10:37 AM
Claude responded: Looking at your console log (document 3), I can see exactly what's happening.
Looking at your console log (document 3), I can see exactly what's happening. The optimizations are working — but there's a new bottleneck that completely dominates the timeline.

The smoking gun is this line:

[CreateCurtainWallsOnAllSlabsCommand] COMPLETE total=3177.1ms
With 11 slabs, the slab loop itself now shows flat, fast times (0.1–0.6ms per slab — the addMany fix worked perfectly). But the total is still 3,177ms. That time is being eaten by _prewarmCurtainWallShaders() running a production scene render with existing geometry.

The comment in your code explains the intent — you moved from an isolated scene to the production scene because WebGPU PSOs are keyed on the full render pass descriptor. But the cost of rendering the production scene (which now contains walls, slabs, 17 walls, shadow FBOs, SSGI, MSAA) is ~800–1,200ms as a synchronous block. For your 11-slab test case with pre-existing geometry, that render call is taking the majority of your 3,177ms.

The second issue is visible here:

[CurtainWallBuilder] §BATCH-CW-PAUSE: resumeAndFlush — 187 walls transferred to pending queue, 1 rAF drain scheduled.
This fires synchronously after runBatch() returns (you can see it appears before signalBuildQueueDrained), meaning Task 3 (defer resumeAndFlush) is not yet implemented in the live code. The BatchCoordinator.ts you shared still has the deferred version in comments/documentation but the console shows it running synchronously.

The third issue: the prewarm is being called inside _processSlabs(), which means it runs inside runBatch(), which means it runs before the loading overlay is visible (the overlay appears when _setupBatch fires, but the render call blocks before the browser can paint). So the user sees a freeze before the spinner even appears.

What to fix:

Move _prewarmCurtainWallShaders() to fire before batchCoordinator.runBatch() is called in execute(), not inside _processSlabs. This way the prewarm happens before the batch starts, but more importantly it separates the prewarm cost from the slab loop timing. If the prewarm itself is still too expensive with a full scene, gate it with a one-time flag — once PSOs are compiled for a session they don't need re-warming on subsequent batches.

typescript
// In execute(), before runBatch:
if (!isRedo && !CreateCurtainWallsOnAllSlabsCommand._shadersPrewarmed) {
    this._prewarmCurtainWallShaders();
    CreateCurtainWallsOnAllSlabsCommand._shadersPrewarmed = true;
}
batchCoordinator.runBatch(_processSlabs, { ... });
Add private static _shadersPrewarmed = false; as a class-level flag so the render call only happens once per browser session. Subsequent batches skip the prewarm entirely since the PSO cache is already warm.

For Task 3, verify the live BatchCoordinator.runBatch() actually contains the scheduleOnce('batch-coordinator-resume-flush', ...) block — the console log shows resumeAndFlush firing synchronously, which means either the deferred version isn't deployed or something is bypassing it.

Good. Now I have the full picture. Let me analyze the screenshot you just shared carefully alongside everything I know.

The screenshot shows the freeze point precisely. Here's what the logs tell me:

What the current logs reveal
What's working ✅

§FIX-SKIP-REDETECT-ROOMS is live and firing correctly — the REDETECT_ROOMS sweep is being skipped for 11 levels
StoreEventBus flushed (depth now 0) — the event bus drain is working
markLevelsDirty already called above — plan-view reprojection hook is correct
The freeze you're seeing in the screenshot happens right at that log line. The browser is frozen because render compiles all deferred shaders — that is the WebGPU PSO compilation render call from _prewarmCurtainWallShaders(), and it is blocking the main thread synchronously while producing that log line.

Precise list of what needs to be done
Fix 1 — One-time prewarm flag (highest priority — causes the freeze)

In CreateCurtainWallsOnAllSlabsCommand.ts:

typescript
// Add at class level:
private static _shadersPrewarmed = false;

// In execute(), BEFORE batchCoordinator.runBatch(...):
if (!isRedo && !CreateCurtainWallsOnAllSlabsCommand._shadersPrewarmed) {
    this._prewarmCurtainWallShaders();
    CreateCurtainWallsOnAllSlabsCommand._shadersPrewarmed = true;
}
// Then call runBatch as normal
Remove the _prewarmCurtainWallShaders() call from inside _processSlabs(). The prewarm will now only run once per browser session. Every subsequent batch (redo, re-run) costs zero.

Fix 2 — Verify deferred resumeAndFlush is actually live

Please share the current BatchCoordinator.ts. The logs from last session showed resumeAndFlush firing synchronously. I need to see whether scheduleOnce('batch-coordinator-resume-flush', ...) is actually in the deployed file or only in a version we discussed.

Fix 3 — Verify requestIdleCallback PBR upgrade is live

Please share initScene.ts (or wherever the post-batch PBR upgrade is triggered). Same question — is the idle deferral actually deployed?

Can you share CreateCurtainWallsOnAllSlabsCommand.ts, BatchCoordinator.ts, and the full console log from this session? Those three will let me give you exact line-by-line diffs for all three fixes.
